The Rational Basis of Continuity Judgment
Definition of continuity judgment and its rational nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the judgment of continuity is a rational judgment, not a sense-based one, and how reason can err in identifying identical existence across time.

Core Idea
Continuity is a rational judgment, not a sense perception.

Continuity—judging that something now is the same as before—may seem obvious, but it is not a judgment that the senses can make. The senses only grasp the present moment; they cannot compare across time. Reason alone can affirm identity across time, but it can also err when it ignores distinguishing features. In this passage, the commentator clarifies this foundational distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the first sentence carefully, which defines the judgment of continuity as asserting that the existent in the second moment is identical to the existent in the first moment.
2
Understand why sense cannot judge
The commentator explains that sense cannot recall two moments, so it cannot compare the existent in them. Reflect on why this makes sense: the senses only perceive the present.
3
Learn about reason's error
Reason errs when it grasps only the commonality between two similar things and misses what distinguishes them. The commentator concludes that blaming sense for such errors is wrong.
This step connects to real-life examples: mistaking two similar objects for the same one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقول : الحكم بالبقاء هو الحكم بأن الموجود في الزمان الثاني هو بعينه الموجود في الزمان الأول ، وهذا الحكم لا يصح من الحس، فإنه لا يقدر على استحضار الزمانين فكيف يستحضر الموجود فيهما ، فإذا الحكم بالبقاء لا يكون إلا من العقل والعقل إنما يغلط إذا عقل المشترك بين الشيئين المتشابهين ولم يعقل ما به يمتاز كل واحد منهما عن الآخر ، فإحالة هذا الغلط على الحس ليس بصواب، وأما حكم الأشاعرة بأن الألوان غير باقية فشيء لزمهم بحسب أصولهم المسلمة عندهم وهى أن الإعدام لا يمكن أن يكون فعلا الفاعل ، وأن الموجود الباقي حال بقائه مستغن عن المؤثر ، وأن لا مؤثر إلا الله تعالى، وإذا شاهدوا أعراضا لايدوم وجودها ألزموا القول بتجددها حالا بعد حال. والمعتزلة لما جوزوا طريان الضد على محل الضد الآخر المقتضى لإفتائه لم يقولوا بذلك ، والفلاسفة لما جعلوا البرقى حال بقائه محتاجا إلى امؤثر لم يحتاجوا إلى ارتكاب ذلك ، والعظام من المعتزلة جمل الأجسام أيضاً غير باقية بمثل ذلك ، وهذه أحكام غير متعلقة بالحس .
I say: The judgment of continuity is the judgment that the existent in the second moment is identical to the existent in the first moment. This judgment is not valid from sense, for it is not capable of recalling the two moments, so how can it recall the existent in them? Thus the judgment of continuity is only from reason. And reason errs only when it grasps the commonality between two similar things and does not grasp that by which each is distinguished from the other. So attributing this error to sense is not correct. As for the Ash'aris' judgment that colors are not permanent, it is something necessitated by their principles as they hold: that non-existences cannot be an act of an agent; that the existent that persists during its continuity is independent of an effect; and that there is no effect except Allah. And when they see accidents that do not persist in existence, they are compelled to say that they are renewed moment after moment. The Mu'tazila, since they allow the occurrence of a contrary to another contrary in a substrate that necessitates its ceasing, did not say that. The philosophers, since they made the persistent (al-baqi) during its continuity need an effect, did not need to resort to that. And the great among the Mu'tazila judged bodies also as not permanent, by similar reasoning. And these are rulings not related to sense.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that distinguishes between sense perception and rational judgment regarding continuity (البقاء). The commentator states that the judgment of continuity—that something existing in the second moment is identical to what existed in the first—is not a sense judgment because the sense cannot compare two moments; it is a rational judgment (من العقل). Reason can err when it only grasps the commonality between two similar things without noticing their distinguishing features. Therefore, blaming the sense for errors in continuity judgments is incorrect. The commentator then explains that the Ash'ari position that colors are non-permanent is derived from their theological principles: that nonexistence cannot be an act, that a persisting existent is independent of an agent during its persistence, and that only Allah is an agent. Since they observe accidents that do not persist, they are forced to say they are renewed continuously. The Mu'tazila, who allow the occurrence of a contrary to a contrary in a substrate (which necessitates the first contrary's annihilation), do not need renewal. The philosophers, who hold that a persistent being still needs an agent during its persistence, also do not need renewal. Some leading Mu'tazila even extend non-persistence to bodies. The conclusion is that these rulings are not based on sense perception but on theoretical principles.

Key Terms
الحكم بالبقاء
الموجود في الزمان الثاني
الحس
العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The senses can judge that something remains the same over time.
Correction: The senses only perceive the present moment; they cannot compare across time. The judgment of continuity requires reason.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is the judgment of continuity not a sense judgment?
A) Sense is unreliable.
B) Sense cannot recall two moments to compare the existent in them.
C) Sense only perceives colors.
D) Reason is more powerful.

Key Takeaway
The judgment of continuity is purely rational; the senses cannot confirm identity across time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you assumed something in your life—a relationship, a belief, your own identity—had remained the same, only to later discover you were mistaken. Was that error due to your senses or your reasoning? What does this passage teach you about the source of such certainty?
?
The passage says reason errs when it grasps only what is common and ignores what is distinct. In your spiritual life, are you focusing on superficial similarities between your faith and others, while neglecting the unique truths that distinguish Islam? What distinction are you most in danger of overlooking?
?
If continuity is a rational judgment, then your own enduring self—the soul that you are—cannot be perceived by the senses. Are you living as if your true identity is your physical body and experiences, or as a rational soul accountable to God? How does this affect your daily choices and your awareness of the Hereafter?

Sectarian Views on Permanence of Accidents
Sectarian applications of rational principles to permanence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari, Mu'tazila, and philosophical principles lead to different conclusions about the permanence of accidents and bodies.

Core Idea
Theological principles, not sense, determine rulings on permanence.

After establishing that judgments of continuity are rational, the commentator examines how different schools—Ash'aris, Mu'tazila, and philosophers—apply rational principles to the permanence of accidents and bodies. Their contrasting conclusions arise from their core theological commitments, not from empirical observation. This section reveals the depth of theoretical reasoning in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ash'ari principles
Read the three principles attributed to the Ash'aris: non-existence cannot be an act, the persistent is independent of an agent during its persistence, and only Allah is an agent.
2
Understand the Ash'ari conclusion
Because they observe accidents that do not persist, and given their principles, they are forced to say accidents are renewed moment by moment.
3
Contrast with Mu'tazila
The Mu'tazila allow the occurrence of a contrary to another contrary in a substrate, which necessitates the annihilation of the first, so they do not need to say accidents are renewed.
4
Note philosophers and leading Mu'tazila
The philosophers hold that the persistent needs an agent during its continuity, so they also do not require renewal. Some leading Mu'tazila extend the same reasoning to bodies, judging them as non-permanent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقول : الحكم بالبقاء هو الحكم بأن الموجود في الزمان الثاني هو بعينه الموجود في الزمان الأول ، وهذا الحكم لا يصح من الحس، فإنه لا يقدر على استحضار الزمانين فكيف يستحضر الموجود فيهما ، فإذا الحكم بالبقاء لا يكون إلا من العقل والعقل إنما يغلط إذا عقل المشترك بين الشيئين المتشابهين ولم يعقل ما به يمتاز كل واحد منهما عن الآخر ، فإحالة هذا الغلط على الحس ليس بصواب، وأما حكم الأشاعرة بأن الألوان غير باقية فشيء لزمهم بحسب أصولهم المسلمة عندهم وهى أن الإعدام لا يمكن أن يكون فعلا الفاعل ، وأن الموجود الباقي حال بقائه مستغن عن المؤثر ، وأن لا مؤثر إلا الله تعالى، وإذا شاهدوا أعراضا لايدوم وجودها ألزموا القول بتجددها حالا بعد حال. والمعتزلة لما جوزوا طريان الضد على محل الضد الآخر المقتضى لإفتائه لم يقولوا بذلك ، والفلاسفة لما جعلوا البرقى حال بقائه محتاجا إلى امؤثر لم يحتاجوا إلى ارتكاب ذلك ، والعظام من المعتزلة جمل الأجسام أيضاً غير باقية بمثل ذلك ، وهذه أحكام غير متعلقة بالحس .
I say: The judgment of continuity is the judgment that the existent in the second moment is identical to the existent in the first moment. This judgment is not valid from sense, for it is not capable of recalling the two moments, so how can it recall the existent in them? Thus the judgment of continuity is only from reason. And reason errs only when it grasps the commonality between two similar things and does not grasp that by which each is distinguished from the other. So attributing this error to sense is not correct. As for the Ash'aris' judgment that colors are not permanent, it is something necessitated by their principles as they hold: that non-existences cannot be an act of an agent; that the existent that persists during its continuity is independent of an effect; and that there is no effect except Allah. And when they see accidents that do not persist in existence, they are compelled to say that they are renewed moment after moment. The Mu'tazila, since they allow the occurrence of a contrary to another contrary in a substrate that necessitates its ceasing, did not say that. The philosophers, since they made the persistent (al-baqi) during its continuity need an effect, did not need to resort to that. And the great among the Mu'tazila judged bodies also as not permanent, by similar reasoning. And these are rulings not related to sense.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that distinguishes between sense perception and rational judgment regarding continuity (البقاء). The commentator states that the judgment of continuity—that something existing in the second moment is identical to what existed in the first—is not a sense judgment because the sense cannot compare two moments; it is a rational judgment (من العقل). According to the commentator, why do the Ash'aris hold that colors are not permanent?
A) They observed colors changing and concluded they are renewed.

C) They deny the sense of sight.
D) They followed the Mu'tazila.

Key Takeaway
Different theological principles yield different conclusions about permanence, all rational rather than empirical.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that your deepest beliefs about God and the world are often based on rational principles you may never have examined. What are the unspoken assumptions you use to make sense of God's actions in your life? Could those assumptions be leading you to a distorted view of His power and mercy?
?
If, like the Ash'aris, you saw that your principles forced you to a conclusion different from what you initially thought, would you be willing to change your principles? Or do you cling to them even if they lead away from the truth?
?
The philosophers held that even a persistent being needs an effect (cause) to continue. How does your awareness of your own continuous need for God's sustaining effect shape your daily trust in Him? Or do you live as if you are 'independent' during good times?

Razi's First Proof: The Impossibility of Sharing Essences
Razi presents his first proof that shared essences lead to impossible transformations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Razi argues that essences cannot be shared, because shared essences would lead to the absurd possibility of the eternal becoming temporal and substances becoming accidents.

Core Idea
Shared essences collapse all differences, making the eternal temporal.

Razi begins his chosen view by attacking the very idea that essences can be shared. If two essences were truly identical in their nature, then whatever is true of one would be true of the other. This would destroy the fundamental distinctions in the world, such as between eternal and originated, substance and accident. Let's examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully.
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the structure: Razi states his chosen view, then gives the reason with a conditional argument.
The passage includes a short commentary in parentheses (2) that reinforces the argument.
2
Identify the key claim and proof.
Razi claims that the view based on the doctrine of states is false. His proof: if essences were shared, then all attributes would be common due to similarity, leading to absurd transformations.
He mentions two schools (Ash'arite and Mu'tazilite) regarding existence, but the argument works regardless.
3
Reflect on the absurd consequences.
The transformation of the eternal into originated and substance into accident is impossible in itself. This shows that the premise (shared essences) must be false.
The commentary gives the example of man and horse sharing animality, which would imply man could turn into a horse.
4
Understand the principle of similarity.
The key logical principle is that similar things have the same necessary concomitants (lawazim). If essences are similar, they must share all properties, eliminating any distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذى أختاره تفريعا على القول بالحال أن ذلك باطل ؛ لأن الذوات لو كانت مشتركة سواء قلنا الوجود الذات على ما يقوله أصحابنا أو غيره على ما يقوله المعتزلة لصح على كل واحد ما يصح على الآخر ضرورة استواء المماثلات في كل اللوازم ، لمكان يلزم صحة انقلاب القديم محدثا والجوهر عرضاً وبالعكس (۲) وهو محال ؛ ولان اختصاص الذات المعينة بالصفة المعينة إن كان لا لأمر فقد ترجح أحد طرفي الممكن على الآخر لا لمرجح وهو محال ، وإن كان الأمر فذاك الأمر إن كان ذاتا عاد البحث في اختصاصها دون سائر الذوات بصفة المرجحية وإن لم يكن ذاتا كان صفة لذات فيعود البحث في اختصاص تلك الذات بها ، أما إذا جعلنا الخصوصية ذاتا وما به الاشتراك صفة اندفع الإشكال لأن الأشياء المختلفة مجوز اشتراكها في لازم واحد ، وأما الأشياء المتساوية فلا يجوز اختلافها في اللوازم (۳) . (۲) أقول : الذي اختاره بعد الفراغ من نقل المذاهب وهو أن الذوات لو كانت مشتركة لام صحة انقلاب القديم محدثا والجوهر عرضاً فوجب أن يكون الحيوانية المشتركة بين الإنسان والفرس تستلزم صحة انقلاب الإنسان فرسا وبالعكس. وجوابه عن هذا جوابهم عما اختاره وأورده عليهم . (۳ ) أقول لهم : أن يقولوا يلزمك في الأجناس والفصول مثل ذلك ، بل في الأشخاص التى تحت نوع واحد ، فإنك إن جعلت الفصول والمشخصات ذواتا والحيوان والإنسان لوازم لما كانت الحيوانية والإنسانية جزء الماهية لا نفسها : فإن اللوازم إنما تلزم بعد تقدم الملزومات، وأيضاً مذهب كثير من المتكلمين أن أحد مقدوريه على الآخر لا المرجح ، فإذا يجوز أن الله تعالى خصص بعض الذوات بصفات من المختار ترجيح
And what I choose as a ramification of the doctrine of the state: that it is false. Because if essences (dhawat) were shared—whether we say existence is the essence, as our companions say, or something else, as the Mu'tazila say—then whatever is true of one would be true of the other, due to the necessity that similars are equal in all concomitants (lawazim). Consequently, it would necessitate the validity of the transformation of the eternal into originated, and the substance into accident, and vice versa (2), which is impossible. And because the specification of a particular essence with a particular attribute, if it is not for a cause, then one of the two sides of the possible would be preferred without a preponderant, which is impossible. And if it is for a cause, then that cause: if it is an essence, the investigation returns to its specification among other essences with the attribute of being a preponderant; and if it is not an essence, then it is an attribute of an essence, so the investigation returns to the specification of that essence with it. However, if we make particularity (al-khususiyya) the essence and that by which there is sharing an attribute, the difficulty is removed, because different things may share one necessary concomitant (lazim), but equal things cannot differ in concomitants (lawazim) (3). (2) I say: what he chose after finishing the transmission of the schools: that if essences were shared, it would necessitate the possibility of the transformation of the eternal into originated, and substance into accident, so it would be necessary that animality shared between man and horse entails the possibility of man turning into a horse and vice versa. And his answer to this is their answer to what he chose and brought against them. (3) I say to them: They would say: the same applies to you concerning genera and differentiae, indeed concerning individuals under one species. For if you make differentiae and individuators (mushakhkhasat) essences, and animality and humanity concurrences (lawazim), then animality and humanity would be part of the quiddity (mahiyya), not the essence itself; for concomitants only follow after the preexistence of the things they accompany. Also, the doctrine of many theologians is that one of two things within God's power is not preponderated [except by God's will], so it is permissible that God Almighty specifies some essences with attributes. From the chosen [view] a preponderance [follows].
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage presents Razi's chosen view on the ramification of the doctrine of states. He argues that the view that essences are shared (i.e., that particularity is an attribute) is false. His proof: if essences were shared and existence were either the essence itself (Ash'arite) or an attribute (Mu'tazilite), then all attributes would be common to all essences, leading to absurdities such as the eternal becoming originated, or substance becoming accident. Furthermore, if a particular essence is specified with a particular attribute without a cause, that would be a preference without a preponderant. If there is a cause, that cause either is an essence (leading to regress) or an attribute of an essence (again regress). The solution, Razi says, is to make particularity (al-khususiyya) the essence itself and the shared aspect an attribute. Then different things can share a concomitant, but equal things cannot differ in concomitants. The two footnotes provide commentary: (2) explains that if essences were shared, it would entail the possibility of transformation (e.g., man to horse), and Razi's answer is parallel to what his opponents say. (3) notes that the same problem applies to genera and differentiae: if they are essences, then the particular would not be part of the quiddity, and the theologians' view of God's specification avoids the problem.

Key Terms
ذوات
مشتركة
قديم
محدث
جوهر
عرض
مماثلات
لوازم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sharing essences is a harmless abstract idea.
Correction: Razi shows it destroys fundamental distinctions like eternal/temporal and substance/accident.

Checkpoint
What absurd consequence does Razi derive from the doctrine of shared essences?
A) God would become ignorant.
B) The eternal could become originated.
C) Humans could become angels.
D) Substances would cease to exist.

Key Takeaway
Razi's first proof shows that shared essences lead to the impossibility of distinguishing the eternal from the temporal, refuting the doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself assuming that God's attributes—like His mercy or power—are essentially the same as human attributes, just bigger? This proof shows that sharing any essence with the eternal leads to absurdity. In what concrete ways do you still unconsciously equate the Creator with His creation? Write down one assumption you hold that blurs this line, and commit to replacing it with the truth from this lesson.
?
If every created thing is radically different in essence from the Eternal, what does that mean for your prayer life? Do you approach God as truly 'other' or do you treat Him as a bigger version of a human helper? How would your worship change if you fully internalized that His essence is utterly unique and incomparable? Make one intentional change in your next prayer that reflects this reality.
?
Razi's argument refutes the idea that you share any essential nature with God. Yet, in moments of pride or self-sufficiency, you act as if you are independent and self-sustaining. Where in your life do you rely on your own strength as if you were eternal? Identify one area of dependence you need to surrender, and ask God to make you acutely aware of your contingency.

Razi's Second Proof and His Solution: Specification and Particularity
Razi presents his second proof based on specification regress and his solution of reversing essence and attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's second argument against shared essences based on the need for a cause of specification, and his solution that particularity is the essence and sharing is an attribute.

Core Idea
Specification without cause is absurd; Razi's solution: make particularity the essence.

Razi advances a second argument: if a particular essence is specified with a particular attribute, this specification must have a cause. If that cause is also an essence, we regress; if it's an attribute, the same problem applies. The only way out is to make the particularity itself the essence, so that what is shared is merely an attribute. This solution also addresses potential objections about genera and species.

Guided Path
1
Read the second argument.
Start with the second part of the passage: the argument about specification without a cause. Follow the two branches.
This argument is independent of the first proof but reinforces the same conclusion.
2
Trace the regress problem.
If specification has a cause that is an essence, we ask about that essence's specification; if it is an attribute, we ask about its essence's specification. This leads to infinite regress.
Razi shows both options lead to the same problem.
3
Understand the solution.
Razi's solution is to reverse the roles: make particularity (khususiyya) the essence and the shared aspect an attribute. Then the regress stops because particularity is foundational.
He argues that different things can share a property without being identical in essence.
4
Consider the footnote objection.
The footnote (3) raises a potential problem regarding genera and differentiae. It says the same issue might apply, but theologians avoid it by making specific attributes subject to divine will.
This footnote shows awareness of objections and provides a response.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذى أختاره تفريعا على القول بالحال أن ذلك باطل ؛ لأن الذوات لو كانت مشتركة سواء قلنا الوجود الذات على ما يقوله أصحابنا أو غيره على ما يقوله المعتزلة لصح على كل واحد ما يصح على الآخر ضرورة استواء المماثلات في كل اللوازم ، لمكان يلزم صحة انقلاب القديم محدثا والجوهر عرضاً وبالعكس (۲) وهو محال ؛ ولان اختصاص الذات المعينة بالصفة المعينة إن كان لا لأمر فقد ترجح أحد طرفي الممكن على الآخر لا لمرجح وهو محال ، وإن كان الأمر فذاك الأمر إن كان ذاتا عاد البحث في اختصاصها دون سائر الذوات بصفة المرجحية وإن لم يكن ذاتا كان صفة لذات فيعود البحث في اختصاص تلك الذات بها ، أما إذا جعلنا الخصوصية ذاتا وما به الاشتراك صفة اندفع الإشكال لأن الأشياء المختلفة مجوز اشتراكها في لازم واحد ، وأما الأشياء المتساوية فلا يجوز اختلافها في اللوازم (۳) . (۲) أقول : الذي اختاره بعد الفراغ من نقل المذاهب وهو أن الذوات لو كانت مشتركة لام صحة انقلاب القديم محدثا والجوهر عرضاً فوجب أن يكون الحيوانية المشتركة بين الإنسان والفرس تستلزم صحة انقلاب الإنسان فرسا وبالعكس. وجوابه عن هذا جوابهم عما اختاره وأورده عليهم . (۳ ) أقول لهم : أن يقولوا يلزمك في الأجناس والفصول مثل ذلك ، بل في الأشخاص التى تحت نوع واحد ، فإنك إن جعلت الفصول والمشخصات ذواتا والحيوان والإنسان لوازم لما كانت الحيوانية والإنسانية جزء الماهية لا نفسها : فإن اللوازم إنما تلزم بعد تقدم الملزومات، وأيضاً مذهب كثير من المتكلمين أن أحد مقدوريه على الآخر لا المرجح ، فإذا يجوز أن الله تعالى خصص بعض الذوات بصفات من المختار ترجيح
And what I choose as a ramification of the doctrine of the state: that it is false. Because if essences (dhawat) were shared—whether we say existence is the essence, as our companions say, or something else, as the Mu'tazila say—then whatever is true of one would be true of the other, due to the necessity that similars are equal in all concomitants (lawazim). Consequently, it would necessitate the validity of the transformation of the eternal into originated, and the substance into accident, and vice versa (2), which is impossible. And because the specification of a particular essence with a particular attribute, if it is not for a cause, then one of the two sides of the possible would be preferred without a preponderant, which is impossible. And if it is for a cause, then that cause: if it is an essence, the investigation returns to its specification among other essences with the attribute of being a preponderant; and if it is not an essence, then it is an attribute of an essence, so the investigation returns to the specification of that essence with it. However, if we make particularity (al-khususiyya) the essence and that by which there is sharing an attribute, the difficulty is removed, because different things may share one necessary concomitant (lazim), but equal things cannot differ in concomitants (lawazim) (3). (2) I say: what he chose after finishing the transmission of the schools: that if essences were shared, it would necessitate the possibility of the transformation of the eternal into originated, and substance into accident, so it would be necessary that animality shared between man and horse entails the possibility of man turning into a horse and vice versa. And his answer to this is their answer to what he chose and brought against them. (3) I say to them: They would say: the same applies to you concerning genera and differentiae, indeed concerning individuals under one species. For if you make differentiae and individuators (mushakhkhasat) essences, and animality and humanity concurrences (lawazim), then animality and humanity would be part of the quiddity (mahiyya), not the essence itself; for concomitants only follow after the preexistence of the things they accompany. Also, the doctrine of many theologians is that one of two things within God's power is not preponderated [except by God's will], so it is permissible that God Almighty specifies some essences with attributes. From the chosen [view] a preponderance [follows].
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage presents Razi's chosen view on the ramification of the doctrine of states. He argues that the view that essences are shared (i.e., that particularity is an attribute) is false. His proof: if essences were shared and existence were either the essence itself (Ash'arite) or an attribute (Mu'tazilite), then all attributes would be common to all essences, leading to absurdities such as the eternal becoming originated, or substance becoming accident. Furthermore, if a particular essence is specified with a particular attribute without a cause, that would be a preference without a preponderant. If there is a cause, that cause either is an essence (leading to regress) or an attribute of an essence (again regress). The solution, Razi says, is to make particularity (al-khususiyya) the essence itself and the shared aspect an attribute. Then different things can share a concomitant, but equal things cannot differ in concomitants. The two footnotes provide commentary: (2) explains that if essences were shared, it would entail the possibility of transformation (e.g., man to horse), and Razi's answer is parallel to what his opponents say. (3) notes that the same problem applies to genera and differentiae: if they are essences, then the particular would not be part of the quiddity, and the theologians' view of God's specification avoids the problem.

ذات
صفة
مرجح
خصوصية
لازم
أجناس
فصول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The regress problem is unsolvable; therefore, the doctrine of states must be true.
Correction: Razi shows the regress only arises if particularity is an attribute; reversing the roles solves it.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, what is the correct way to avoid the regress problem in specifying essences with attributes?
A) Affirm that essences are shared and attributes are particular.
B) Make particularity (al-khususiyya) the essence and the shared aspect an attribute.
C) Deny that attributes exist at all.
D) Claim that all specifications are by divine will with no further explanation.

Key Takeaway
Razi solves the specification regress by making particularity the essence and shared attributes mere properties, preserving distinctions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you try to justify a belief or action by citing a cause, do you ever realize that cause itself needs justification, leading to an infinite chain? How does Razi's argument about specification expose the arbitrariness of any worldview that lacks a foundational cause? Will you commit to grounding your life on the uncreated Word of Allah rather than on unexamined preferences?
?
Razi's solution requires reversing what seems natural: making particularity primary and shared attributes secondary. In your own spiritual life, is there an area where you prioritize generic practices (like rituals) over your unique relationship with Allah? What would it mean to make your individual connection with Allah the essence, and let all practices flow as necessary concomitants from that?

Three Properties of the Necessary Being
The author lists three properties of the Necessary Being.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three rational properties of the Necessary Being: that it cannot be necessary by itself and for another simultaneously, that it is not composed, and that it does not have a composite from it.

Core Idea
The Necessary Being is simple, independent, and not part of anything else.

The author begins enumerating the properties (khawass) of the Necessary Being. Although he states there are ten, this passage covers the first three. These properties establish that the Necessary Being is absolutely independent and simple, free from composition or being a part of anything.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the meaning.
The passage uses very concise argumentation. Pay attention to the logical connectors.
2
Understand the first property
The first issue: a thing cannot be necessary by itself and by another at the same time. The reason given is that what is by another ceases with that other, while what is by itself does not. Combining the two is impossible.
This demonstrates that necessity by itself is absolute and independent.
3
Understand the second property
The second issue: the Necessary Being is not composed of parts. The reasoning: every composite needs its parts, and parts are other than itself; needing another implies possibility, but the Necessary Being is impossible.
This shows that composition implies dependence, which contradicts necessity.
4
Understand the third property
The third issue: the Necessary Being does not have another composed from it. That is, it is not a part or constituent of some other composite being.
This emphasizes that God is not a component of any created thing.
5
Reflect on independence
Consider how these three properties collectively establish that the Necessary Being is self-sufficient, simple, and not dependent on or part of anything else.
This is foundational for understanding divine transcendence in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خواص الواجب لذاته وهى عشرة ) مسألة : الشيء الواحد لا يكون واجبا لذاته ولغيره معا ) الان ما بالغير يرتفع بارتفاع الغير وما بالذات لا يرتفع بارتفاع الغير والجمع بينهما محال . ( مسألة : الواجب لذاته لا يتركب عن غيره ) الان كل مركب محتاج إلى جزئه وجزؤه غيره وكل مركب محتاج إلى غيره ممكن لذاته ولا شيء من الممكن لذاته واجب لذاته + مسألة : الواجب لذاته لا يتركب عنه غيره )
Properties of the Necessary Being—they are ten. Issue: One thing cannot be necessary by itself and necessary for another simultaneously. The reason: what is by another ceases with the cessation of the other, while what is by itself does not cease with the cessation of the other; combining them is impossible. Issue: The Necessary Being is not composed of another. The reason: every composite is in need of its part, and its part is other than it, and every composite is in need of another, and everything in need of another is possible by itself, and nothing possible by itself is necessary by itself. Issue: The Necessary Being does not have another composed from it.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage enumerates properties of the Necessary Being. Although the author states there are ten, only three are provided. The first property: a thing cannot be necessary by itself and also necessary through another simultaneously, because these two modes have opposite implications (permanence vs. dependence). The second property: the Necessary Being is not composed of parts, because composition entails need for parts, and need entails possibility, which contradicts necessity. The third property: the Necessary Being does not have a composite arising from it (i.e., it is not a constituent part of something else).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The third property means God does not create composite things or that God cannot be part of a composite in any sense.
Correction: The third property specifically means that God is not a constituent part of any composite being, nor does He emanate a composite from His essence. It does not deny that God creates composite things; rather it safeguards His transcendence.

Checkpoint
According to the second property, why can't the Necessary Being be composed of parts?
A) Because every composite is possible and the Necessary Being is not possible
B) Because God does not have parts in His essence
C) Because composition implies need, and need implies possibility, which contradicts necessity
D) Both A and C

Key Takeaway
The Necessary Being is absolutely simple and independent, free from composition and from being part of anything else.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This lesson says God is not composed of parts. Do you ever subconsciously think of God's mercy as separate from His justice, as if He is pulled in different directions? How does affirming His simplicity change the way you approach His attributes?
?
If God is not a part of any composite, then He is not a 'piece' of your life to be balanced with other priorities. Are you living as if God is one item on a list, or as if He is the entire ground of your existence? What would change about your daily routine if you truly believed this?

The one thing cannot be necessary in itself and through another
Imam Razi states the first property: a single thing cannot be necessary both in itself and through another.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a single entity cannot be simultaneously necessary in itself and necessary through another, and the logical proof behind this impossibility.

Core Idea
Self-necessity and derived necessity are mutually exclusive by their very nature.

Before we delve into the attributes of Allah, we must establish the fundamental rules of necessity. Imam Razi begins with a key property: a single thing cannot be both intrinsically necessary and necessarily dependent on another. This distinction is crucial for understanding the uniqueness of Allah's existence. Let's examine his concise proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to feel its structure, then read the English translation. Notice the logical flow from statement to proof.
The passage is short but dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two types of necessity
The passage mentions 'necessary in itself' (wajib li-dhatihi) and 'necessary through another' (wajib li-ghayrihi). Understand the difference: one is intrinsic, the other depends on something else.
These terms are central to kalam discussions on God's attributes.
3
Understand the proof
The proof hinges on the behavior of each type: what is through another ceases when that other ceases; what is in itself does not. This contradiction makes combination impossible.
Focus on the logical impossibility, not just theological inheritance.
4
Test your understanding with the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to check if you grasped the core reasoning. Use the passage as your only reference.
If you answer incorrectly, review the commentary and translation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : الشيء الواحد لا يكون واجبا لذاته ولغيره معا . الان ما بالغير يرتفع بارتفاع الغير وما بالذات لا يرتفع بارتفاع الغير والجمع بينهما محال
Issue: The one thing cannot be necessary in itself and through another simultaneously. Because that which is through another ceases with the cessation of the other, and that which is in itself does not cease with the cessation of the other, and combining them is impossible.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of a property. Imam Razi states that a single entity cannot have both self-necessity (wājib bi-dhātihī) and necessity through another (wājib bi-ghayrihī) at the same time. The proof is simple: that which is necessary through another depends on that other for its necessity—if the other ceases, its necessity ceases. But that which is necessary in itself does not depend on anything; its necessity is intrinsic and cannot cease. Therefore, these two modes of necessity are mutually exclusive, and their combination in one thing is impossible.

Key Terms
واجب لذاته
واجب لغيره
ارتفاع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that a thing can be necessary in itself and through another in different respects (e.g., necessary in itself in one aspect and necessary through another in another aspect).
Correction: Imam Razi's proof shows that the two types of necessity are defined by their independence or dependence. A single entity cannot have both an independent and a dependent origin for its necessity, as that would imply it both does and does not rely on something else for its necessity.

Checkpoint
Why can't one thing be necessary in itself and through another at the same time?
A) Because everything necessary through another is actually necessary in itself.
B) Because what is necessary through another ceases when the other ceases, while what is necessary in itself does not.
C) Because necessary existence cannot be shared between two modes.
D) Because necessity is a simple attribute that cannot be divided.

Key Takeaway
A single entity cannot combine essential necessity and derived necessity because they have opposite dependencies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever placed your ultimate trust in something that could be taken away? How does knowing that only the One who is necessary in Himself never cease help you reorient your heart today?
?
If your own sense of worth or security depends on anything but Allah, what specific step will you take this week to shift that dependence to Him alone?
?
The proof shows that a thing that is necessary through another is not truly independent. In what areas of your life are you treating temporary things as if they are permanent, and what would it cost you to let go of that illusion?

The Necessary's Existence Not Additional to Its Essence
Imam Razi proves the fourth property: existence is not an accident added to the essence of the Necessary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Razi argues that the existence of the Necessary Being cannot be an accident added to its essence, and the rational consequences of that position.

Core Idea
Existence cannot be an extra attribute because that leads to circularity or infinite regress.

This passage tackles a subtle but critical point in Islamic theology: Is God’s existence something added to His essence, or is it identical with it? Imam Razi presents a rigorous proof that superaddition is impossible, using a dilemma that exposes logical contradictions. The argument is foundational for the Ash'ari doctrine that God's attributes are not distinct from His essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Let the author's own argument flow before interpreting.
The passage is dense; you may need to read slowly.
2
Identify the main dilemma
Notice that Razi presents two possibilities for an additional existence: independent of essence (then not an attribute) or dependent (then contingent). Focus on the second branch.
This sets up the core of the proof.
3
Trace the regress argument
Follow the reasoning under the dependent branch: the cause cannot be other (else necessary through another) nor the essence itself (leads to circularity, duplication, or infinite regress).
Each step eliminates a possible cause.
4
Examine the objection and response
Consider the objection that the essence causes existence without being conditioned by existence. Note how Razi responds by comparing to the contingent's essence.
This strengthens the argument by showing the objection fails.
5
Reflect on the final epistemological point
The last sentence appears to support the opposite view. Discuss in context whether it is a counterargument or part of the proof.
This requires careful interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : الواجب الذاته لا يكون وجوده زائدا على ماهيته . لان ذلك الوجود إن كان مستغنيا عن تلك الماهية لم يكن صفة لها وإن لم يكن مستغنيا كان ممكنا لذاته مفتقرا إلى مؤثر وذلك المؤثر إن كان غير تلك الماهية كان الواجب لذاته واجبا لغيره ، وإن كان تلك الماهية فهى حال إيها بها ذلك الوجوب ، إما أن تكون موجودة أولا تكون، والأول محال لأنها لو كانت موجودة بهذا الوجود كان الوجود الواحد شرط نفسه وإن كانت بغيره كانت الماهية موجودة مرتين ، ثم الكلام في ذلك الوجود كالكلام في الأول فيلزم التسلسل ، وإن لم تكن موجودة فهو محال لانا لو جوزنا كون المعدوم مؤثرا في الوجود لم يمكنا الاستدلال بفاعلية الله تعالى على وجوده ، ولان تأثير المعدوم في الموجود باطل بالبديهة . لاعتراض لم لا يجوز أن يكون المؤثر فيه و الماهية لا بشرط الوجود ، ثم لا يلزم من حذف الوجود من دريمة الاعتبار دخول العدم فيها ، لأن المساعية من حيث هي لا موجودة ولا معدومة، وهذا كما قالوا في الممكن فإن ماهيته قابلة الوجود لا بشرط وجود آخر وإلا وقع التسلسل ، ولم يلزم أيضاً أن يكون القابل لوجود معدر ما وإلا لزم كون الشيء الواحد في الوقت الواحد موجودا معدوما معا؟ ثم الذى يدل على أن وجود واجب لوجود زائد على ماهيته أن وجوده معلوم وماهيته غير معلومة والمعلوم غير ما ليس بمعلوم
Issue: The Necessary in itself: its existence is not additional to its essence. Because that existence, if it were independent of that essence, would not be an attribute of it; and if it were not independent, it would be contingent in itself, in need of an effecter. That effecter, if it were other than that essence, then the Necessary in itself would be necessary through another; and if it were that essence, then it [the essence] when giving that existence is either existent or not existent. The first is impossible, because if it were existent through this existence, then the one existence would be a condition of itself; and if it were [existent] through another, then the essence would be existent twice. Then the discussion about that existence is like the discussion about the first, so an infinite regress follows. If it were not existent, that is impossible, because if we allowed the non-existent to be an effecter in existence, we could not infer God's agency from His existence; and because the effect of the non-existent on the existent is intuitively false. One might object: why not allow that the effecter is the essence without the condition of existence? Then it does not follow from removing existence from the consideration [؟] that non-existence enters into it, because the essence [؟] as such is neither existent nor non-existent. This is like what they said about the contingent: its essence is receptive of existence without the condition of another existence, otherwise an infinite regress would occur; and it also does not follow that the receptive of existence is non-existent, otherwise one thing would be existent and non-existent at the same time. Then what indicates that the existence of the Necessary is additional to its essence is that His existence is known and His essence is unknown, and the known is other than what is not known.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the Necessary's existence is not a superadded attribute (zā'id) to its essence. Imam Razi presents a dilemma: if existence were additional, it would either be independent of the essence (then it wouldn't be an attribute) or dependent (then it would be contingent, needing a cause). That cause cannot be other than the essence (otherwise the Necessary would be necessary through another), nor can it be the essence itself, because that leads to either circularity (existence conditioning itself) or duplication (existence twice), or infinite regress. Even if one tries to say the essence gives existence without being existent, that would allow the non-existent to be a cause, which is absurd and would undermine the proof of God's existence from His agency. The argument also addresses a potential objection that the essence can be a cause without being conditioned by existence, similar to how the contingent's essence is receptive of existence without being existent. Finally, he notes a proof from epistemology: we know that God exists but do not comprehend His essence, so existence is known while essence is unknown, indicating distinction. However, this last point is presented as a proof for the opposite position (that existence is additional), but in the context it seems to be mentioned as a point to be refuted or considered.

Key Terms
وجود زائد
ماهية
علة
تسلسل
قابل الوجود
فاعلية الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think that if existence is not additional, then God's existence and essence are identical, which would mean we can fully know His essence.
Correction: Razi's argument is that existence cannot be a superadded accident, but he does not claim that essence and existence are identical. The argument is about logical impossibility of addition, not about identity.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason Imam Razi gives for why the existence of the Necessary cannot be additional to its essence?
A) Because if existence were additional, it would lead to an infinite regress or circularity.
B) Because existence and essence are identical in God.
C) Because the essence does not know itself.
D) Because existence is a simple concept that cannot be added.

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi's proof demonstrates that the Necessary's existence cannot be a superadded attribute, as any attempt to add existence leads to logical absurdities such as circularity, duplication, or infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the fact that God's existence is not an added attribute but is His very essence, how does that challenge the way you sometimes think of God as having 'parts' or separate qualities? Are you guilty of mentally dividing God into a collection of attributes rather than worshipping the One whose existence is simple and absolute? How will you correct this in your next prayer?
?
The argument warns against assuming that existence can be added to the essence, which would lead to an infinite regress. In your own life, where do you see yourself chasing after things that are merely additional, thinking they will complete you, while ignoring the reality that your very existence is already dependent on the Necessary? What are the 'additional' pursuits that are distracting you from the essential?
?
Razi says that if we allowed the non-existent to be an effecter, we could not infer God's agency from His existence. Do you ever treat God as if He is not actively present in every moment, as if He is a distant cause? How does this proof call you to see God's agency in your daily existence, not as something extra but as the very ground of your being?

The Necessity of the Necessary is Not an Added Attribute
Imam Razi proves the fifth property: necessity is not additional.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Razi argues that the necessity of the Necessary Being cannot be an additional attribute distinct from its essence.

Core Idea
If necessity were additional, it would lead to absurd priority relations.

Imam Razi continues to establish the properties of the Necessary Being. Here he tackles a subtle point: is the necessity (wujūb) itself an extra attribute added to the essence? He argues that such a view leads to logical contradictions. Let's follow his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage aloud or silently. Notice the concise style and the conditional structure 'إذا لو كان...'. The passage is incomplete, but the core argument is clear.
The text cuts off at the end, but the direction of the argument is still understandable.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
The passage presents a dilemma: if necessity were additional, it either follows existence or is followed by existence. Identify each horn and its consequence.
Horn 1: necessity follows existence → branch is origin for origin. Horn 2: necessity is followed → necessity becomes contingent.
3
Understand why both horns are impossible
For horn 1, the branch (necessity) cannot be the origin of the origin (existence). For horn 2, if necessity is contingent, then the Necessary would be contingent, which is a contradiction.
The second horn implies that what is necessary in itself would be contingent in itself, which is absurd.
4
Conclude the proof
Since both possibilities are impossible, the original assumption (that necessity is additional) must be false. Therefore, necessity is not an added attribute.
Even though the text is incomplete, the logical structure is complete enough to draw this conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : الواجب لذاته لا يجوز أن يكون وجوبه زائداً عليه . إذ لو كان زائداً فإن كان الوجوب تابعا للوجود لزم الفرع أصلا للأصل وهو محال ، وإن كان تابعا لزم أن يكون ممكنا لذاته واجبا بغيره فيكون الوجوب بالذات ممكنا بالذات فيكون الواجب لذاته أولى أن
Issue: The Necessary in itself: it is not permissible for its necessity to be additional to it. Because if it were additional, then if necessity follows existence, then the branch would be an origin for the origin, which is impossible; and if it is followed [by existence], then it would be contingent in itself and necessary through another, so the necessary in itself would be contingent in itself, so the Necessary in itself would be more deserving that ...
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a proof that necessity (wujūb) is not an additional attribute of the Necessary. Imam Razi presents a two-part argument: if necessity were additional, either it follows existence (i.e., existence is prior and necessity consequent) or it is followed by existence (necessity prior). The first option makes the branch (necessity) an origin for the origin (existence), which is absurd. The second option makes necessity itself contingent and necessary through another, which contradicts it being essential. The argument is truncated but the direction is clear.

Key Terms

زائد
تابع
فرع
أصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that necessity and existence are two distinct attributes of God, like power and knowledge.
Correction: Imam Razi shows that if they were distinct, priority relations would lead to absurdity. Necessity is not an added attribute; it is identical with the essence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can't necessity be additional to the Necessary?
A) Because necessity and existence are the same thing.
B) Because if necessity were additional, it would either be prior or posterior to existence, both of which are absurd.
C) Because additional attributes lead to multiplicity in God, which is impossible.
D) Because necessity is a relative concept that cannot be an attribute.

Key Takeaway
The necessity of the Necessary cannot be an added attribute because any such addition leads to absurd priority relations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God’s necessity were not inherent but an added attribute, He would be contingent. When you face trials, do you ever secretly doubt whether God will ‘remain’ necessary to sustain you? How does that doubt reflect a misunderstanding of His necessity being identical to His essence?
?
The proof shows that necessity cannot be separate from God’s essence. In your worship, do you sometimes treat God’s faithfulness or mercy as ‘add-ons’ that He might lose? How would it change your reliance to remember they are not separate but essential to who He is?
?
You say ‘Allah is Necessary.’ But what if you truly internalized that His necessity is not a property He earned or could lose? Would you still fear that your sins could diminish His mercy, or that your good deeds could increase His love? Answer honestly: Do you act as if God’s attributes are conditional on you?

Proof that Existence is Not Additional to God's Essence
Razi presents a proof against existence being additional to quiddity of the Necessary Being.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's logical proof that existence is not a superadded attribute of the Necessary Being, and why the alternative leads to circularity or infinite regress.

Core Idea
God's existence is identical to His essence, not a separate attribute.

In this passage, Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents a tight logical argument to refute the idea that God's existence is something added to His essence (quiddity). Such a view was held by some theologians, but Razi demonstrates that it leads to impossible consequences. Follow his reasoning carefully, as each step eliminates a possible scenario until only the conclusion remains.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem
The issue: is God's existence an additional attribute (like whiteness) or identical to His essence? Before reading the proof, know that the claim being refuted is that existence is superadded.
This question applies only to God; for contingent things, existence is additional.
2
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Try to follow the flow of the argument without worrying about every detail yet.
The argument uses conditional statements (if...then...).
3
Identify the conditional branches
Notice the two main cases: the additional existence is either independent of the quiddity or dependent. Each leads to a problem. Then within the dependent case, the cause must be either other than the quiddity or the quiddity itself, both leading to absurdities.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum argument.
4
Recognize the conclusions
The argument concludes that the initial assumption (existence is additional) is false. Therefore, existence and quiddity are one in the Necessary Being.
This is a key doctrine in Islamic theology regarding divine simplicity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لان ذلك الوجود إن كان مستغنيا عن تلك الماهية لم يكن صفة لها وإن لم يكن مستغنيا كان ممكنا لذاته مفتقرا إلى مؤثر وذلك المؤثر إن كان غير تلك الماهية كان الواجب لذاته واجبا لغيره ، وإن كان تلك الماهية فهى حال إيها بها ذلك الوجوب ، إما أن تكون موجودة أولا تكون، والأول محال لأنها لو كانت موجودة بهذا الوجود كان الوجود الواحد شرط نفسه وإن كانت بغيره كانت الماهية موجودة مرتين ، ثم الكلام في ذلك اللوجود كال كلام فى الأول فيلزم التسلسل
Because that existence, if it were independent of that quiddity, would not be an attribute of it; and if it were not independent, it would be possible in itself, in need of an efficient cause. And that efficient cause, if it were other than that quiddity, then the Necessary in Himself would be necessary through another. And if it were that quiddity, then when it bestows that necessity on it, either it is existent or not existent. The first is impossible, because if it were existent by this existence, then the one existence would be a condition of itself; and if it were [existent] by something else, the quiddity would exist twice. Then the discussion about that existence is like the discussion about the first, so an infinite regress follows.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a proof: the author argues that the existence of the Necessary Being cannot be additional to His quiddity. The argument proceeds by supposing that existence is additional. If that additional existence is independent of the quiddity, it is not a real attribute; if it is dependent, then it is contingent and requires a cause. That cause cannot be other than the quiddity (otherwise the Necessary would be necessary through another), nor can it be the quiddity itself, because the quiddity would then have to be existent prior to bestowing existence, leading to circularity or a double existence, and ultimately an infinite regress. The conclusion is that existence is not a superadded attribute.

Key Terms
وجود
ماهية
واجب لذاته
علة
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God's existence is an attribute added to His essence, just like existence is added to the essences of created things.
Correction: Razi's proof shows that if that were the case, it would lead to absurdities such as circularity and infinite regress. Hence for God, existence is identical to His essence.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, if the quiddity bestows existence on itself, what problem arises?
A) The quiddity must be existent before bestowal, causing circularity or double existence.
B) The quiddity becomes impossible.
C) The quiddity is independent of existence.
D) The quiddity is caused by another.

Key Takeaway
Razi demonstrates that the assumption of existence being additional to God's essence leads to logical absurdities, proving that for the Necessary Being, existence and quiddity are one.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about God's existence, do you ever unconsciously imagine it as a separate 'thing' added to His essence, like an attribute? How does Razi's logical demolition of that assumption challenge you to purify your understanding of God's oneness?
?
If your own existence is contingent—needing a cause—how does reflecting on God's necessary existence, where essence and existence are one, change the way you see your absolute dependence on Him in every moment?
?
Razi shows that any distinction in God leads to contradictions. Examine your heart: are there areas where you subtly treat God's attributes as separate parts (e.g., His mercy vs. His justice)? How does this lesson call you to a simpler, more unified worship of His indivisible reality?

Razi's Refutation and Alternative Proof on Divine Existence
Razi criticizes a previous argument and provides an alternative proof for non-addition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's critique of the argument that God's existence is additional to His essence, and his own proof from the impossibility of multiplicity in the First Principle.

Core Idea
Razi argues that God's existence is not separate from His essence because multiplicity is impossible in the First Principle.

In this passage, Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi takes on a key argument from his predecessors that claims God's existence is additional to His essence. He first critiques the premises used, then provides his own proof from the impossibility of multiplicity in the First Principle. By following his reasoning, we see how kalam thinkers defended divine simplicity.

Guided Path
1
Read the critique of the relation argument
Identify Razi's objection to the notion of 'relation' used in the previous proof. Note how he distinguishes permissible and impossible meanings of composition.
He allows logical composition but denies physical mixture.
2
Examine the rejection of quiddity as cause
Razi argues that quiddity cannot be a cause for existence without itself existing. Grasp the rational intuition he invokes.
This is a key move against those who posit quiddity as a separate reality.
3
Understand the alternative proof from multiplicity
Razi provides his own proof: multiplicity requires principles, so the First Principle cannot have any multiplicity. That means existence cannot be additional.
This is a concise argument for divine simplicity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(1) أقول : لا أدرى أى شيء يعنى هذه العلاقة فإن الواجب له علاقة العلية والمبدئية بالغير ، وإن أراد بالتركيب الانضمام إلى الغير في مثل قولها الموجودات بأسرها والواجب المطلق الشامل للواجب بالذات و بالغير فهو جائز ، وإن أراد أن يكون بينه وبين غيره فعل وانفعال كما في الممتزجات فمحال عليه لأنه لا ينفعل عن غيره . (٢) أقول : هذا الاعتراض هو مذهبه الذى يدعيه فى سائر كتبه ، ولاشك أن الماهية من حيث هي لصفة معقولة لها ، كما أن ماهية الالذين علة لزوجيتها أما كون من حيث هى هى علة لوجود أو موجود فمحال لان بديهة العقل حاكمة بوجوب كون ماهو علة لوجود موجود وليس كذلك في قبول الوجود ، فإن قابل الوجود يستحيل أن يكون موجودا وإلا فيحصل له ماهو حاصل له . وأما الاستدلال على كون وجوده زائدا على ماهيته بأن وجوده معلوم وماهيته غير معلومة فغير صحيح ؛ وجوده المعلوم هو المشترك بينه وبين غيره وهو أمر معقول يقع عليه وعلى غيره بالتشكيك والذي هو غير معلوم هو وجوده الخارجي الخاص به القائم بذاته الذى لا يمكن أن تعمل على غيره . والدليل على استحالة كون وجوده زائدا على ماهيته هو استحالة وقوع الكثرة فيه بوجه ، فإن كل كثرة محتاجة إلى مبادى فبدأ المبادى لا يكون فيه كثرة بوجه من الوجوه أصلا .
(1) I say: I do not know what he means by this relation, for the Necessary has a relation of causality and origination to others. If he means by composition the joining to another, like saying 'all existents' and 'the absolute Necessary encompassing the necessary by essence and by other', then it is permissible. If he means that between it and another there is action and passion as in mixtures, that is impossible for Him because He is not affected by another. (2) I say: This objection is his doctrine that he claims in all his books. There is no doubt that the quiddity in itself has an intelligible attribute, just as the quiddity of ... is a cause for its evenness. As for its being in itself a cause for existence or existent, that is impossible, because the intuition of reason rules that what is a cause for existence must exist, and that is not the case for the recipient of existence; indeed, the recipient of existence cannot be existent, otherwise it would obtain what it already has. As for the inference that His existence is additional to His quiddity because His existence is known and His quiddity is unknown, it is unsound. His known existence is the commonality between Him and others—a intelligible concept predicated of Him and others by analogy—and what is unknown is His particular external existence subsisting by itself which cannot be ... . The proof for the impossibility of His existence being additional to His quiddity is the impossibility of any multiplicity in Him, for every multiplicity requires principles, so the First Principle cannot have any multiplicity whatsoever.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a critique and counter-argument. The author (Razi) first dismisses a premise about relation used in the previous proof: the Necessary has a causal relation to others, but composition understood as physical mixture is denied. He then rejects the objection that quiddity can be a cause for existence while being non-existent, citing rational intuition. He also refutes the argument from knowledge: that we know God's existence but not His quiddity—this only shows a conceptual distinction, not ontological addition. Finally, he provides a positive argument: multiplicity in God is impossible because He is the First Principle, and all multiplicity depends on principles. Therefore, existence cannot be additional.

Key Terms
علاقة
علة
تشكيك
كثرة
مبدأ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Knowing God's existence while not knowing His quiddity proves that existence is an additional attribute to His essence.
Correction: Razi explains that the known existence is only a common, analogical concept, not His real, particular existence. Therefore, no real addition is established.

Checkpoint
Why does Razi reject the inference that existence is additional because existence is known and quiddity unknown?
A) He denies that existence is known.
B) He says the known existence is a common concept, not the specific external existence.
C) He says quiddity is always known.
D) He says the inference is valid but irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
Razi refutes the addition argument and establishes divine simplicity by showing that multiplicity cannot exist in the First Principle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Razi argues that God's existence is not separate from His essence—there is no division in Him. What would it look like for you to surrender to God's unified decree this week?
?
The lesson distinguishes between the common concept of existence (shared by all existents) and God's particular existence. Are you content to know God only through a shared concept, or do you yearn to know Him as He is in Himself—beyond analogy? Proof That Necessity Is Not Additional to God's Essence
Razi presents a proof against necessity being an added attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that the attribute of necessity (Wujub) cannot be an additional attribute distinct from the essence of the Necessary Being.

Core Idea
If necessity were additional, it would lead to impossible contradictions or infinite regress.

Imam Razi, a master of rational theology, argues that the very attribute of 'necessity' that defines the Necessary Being cannot be a separate addition to His essence. He uses a clever disjunctive argument to show that whether necessity depends on existence or is independent, both paths lead to absurdity. Then he adds a regress argument. Let's unpack this dense proof step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the original Arabic and its English translation. Notice the conditional structure (لو كان).
The passage has two main parts: a disjunctive argument and a regress argument.
2
Understand the disjunctive assumption
The argument assumes necessity is additional. Then it splits into two possibilities: necessity follows existence or necessity precedes existence.
Each possibility leads to a contradiction.
3
Analyze the first horn: necessity follows existence
If necessity (branch) follows existence (root), then the branch would be prior to the root, which is impossible in causal relationships.
This shows that necessity cannot be a result of existence.
4
Analyze the second horn: necessity precedes existence
If necessity precedes existence, then necessity itself becomes contingent (because it depends on a cause to bring it about). This would make the Necessary Being contingent in that respect, which is contradictory.
The argument uses the principle that what is necessary through another is contingent in itself.
5
Examine the regress argument
If the necessity of the first necessity requires another necessity, then an infinite regress of necessities follows, which is impossible.
This seals the argument: necessity cannot be additional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذ لو كان زائداً فإن كان الوجوب ستتبعا الوجود السكان الفرع أصلا للأصل وهو محال ، وإن كان تابعا لزم أن يكون ممكنا لذاته واجبا بغيره فيكون الوجوب بالذات ممكنا بالذات فيكون الواجب لذاته أولى أن يكون ممكنا لذاته ، وأيضاً فوجوب ذلك الوجوب يكون لوجوب مؤثره على هذا التقدير ، فقبل هذا الوجوب وجوب آخر لا إلى غاية ، ولزم التسلسل وهو محال
For if it were additional, then if the necessity were consequent upon existence, the branch would be prior to the root, which is impossible; and if it were dependent, then it would be contingent in itself and necessary through another, so necessity by essence would be contingent by essence, making the Necessary in Himself more deserving of being contingent in Himself. Also, the necessity of that necessity would be for the necessity of its efficient cause on this supposition, so before this necessity there would be another necessity ad infinitum, leading to an infinite regress, which is impossible.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage contains a proof that necessity (وجوب) is not an additional attribute over the essence of the Necessary Being. The argument is disjunctive: if necessity were additional, it either follows existence (contradiction: branch precedes root) or precedes existence (making necessity itself contingent and dependent on a cause, then necessity-by-essence becomes contingent). Additionally, if necessity requires a cause, then each necessity would require a prior necessity, leading to infinite regress. Thus, necessity is not additional.

Key Terms
وجوب
وجود
تابع
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the necessity of God is a separate attribute like 'power' or 'knowledge' that is added to His essence.
Correction: Razi shows that necessity cannot be added because it would lead to logical contradictions; rather, necessity is identical to God's essence.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's argument, if necessity were additional and dependent on existence, what would be the consequence?
A) Necessity would be necessary by essence.
B) The Necessary Being would be contingent by essence.
C) Existence would be added to necessity.
D) No consequence.

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi proves that the necessity of the Necessary Being cannot be a separate attribute, as it would lead to logical contradictions and infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's necessity is not an added attribute but identical to His essence, then your entire existence is contingent upon a Being whose very nature is necessary. Are you living as if you are self-sufficient, or do you constantly acknowledge your dependence on the Necessary Being? What would change if you truly internalized that you are contingent by essence?
?
Razi shows that treating necessity as separate leads to absurdity. Is there any attribute of God that you tend to think of as separate from His essence, diminishing His absolute oneness? How can you guard your heart against dividing God's attributes in worship?
?
The proof uses an infinite regress to show that nothing can cause its own necessity. In your daily life, do you ever seek ultimate security in things that themselves depend on others—like wealth, status, or relationships? How can you redirect your trust solely to the Necessary Being, who depends on nothing?

Why Necessary Existence Cannot Be Shared
Razi's proof that necessity cannot be shared

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why necessary existence cannot be a common attribute shared between two beings, based on Razi's proof from composition and infinite regress.

Core Idea
Sharing necessary existence forces composition, dependence, or contradiction.

Razi presents a rigorous proof that necessary existence cannot be a shared attribute. If it were shared, each being would be composite of a common factor (necessity) and a distinguishing factor, leading to unacceptable consequences. This lesson walks through that proof step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Focus on understanding the flow of the argument: the conditional structure and the contradictions that arise.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the composition dilemma
Identify the two cases: either there is no necessary connection between the parts (leading to an external cause) or there is a necessary connection (leading to two sub-cases: essence entails necessity or necessity entails essence).
Each case leads to a contradiction with necessary existence.
3
Grasp the infinite regress argument
The final part uses the assumption that existence is a positive attribute. If so, existence is other than the quiddity, leading to an infinite regress or the necessary being becoming contingent.
This reinforces the impossibility of shared necessary existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإلا لكان هو مغايرا لما به يمتاز كل واحد منهما عن الآخر فيكون كل واحد منهما مركبا عما به الاشتراك وما به الامتياز ، فإن لم يسكن بين الجزئية ملازمة كان اجتماعهما معلول علة منفصلة هذا خلف ، وإن كان بينهما ملازمة فإن استلزمت الهوية للوجوب كان الوجوب محلول الغير هذا خلاف ، وإن كان الوجوب مستلزما لتلك الهوية فكل واجب هو هو ما ليس هو لم يكن واجبا فقيل عليه بناء على كون الوجود وصفا ثبوتيا وهو باطل وإلا لسكان داخلا في الماهية أو خارجا وكلاهما باطلان على ما تقدم ، ولأنه لو كان ثبوتيا لمكان مساويا فى الثبوت كسائر الماهيات ومخالفا لها فى خصوصيته فوجوده غير ماهيته فاتصاف ماهيته بوجوده إن كان واجبا كان الوجوب وجوب آخر إلى غير النهاية ، وإن لم يكن واجبا كان ممكنا والواجب أداته أولى أن يكون ممكنا هذا خلف
Otherwise it would be different from that by which each one is distinguished from the other, so each one would be composed of what is shared and what distinguishes. If there is no necessary connection between the parts, their composition would be caused by a separate cause—this is a [vicious] circle. If there is a necessary connection, then if the essence entails necessity, necessity would be dependent on another—this is contrary [to necessity]. If necessity entails that essence, then every necessary being would be itself not itself; it would not be necessary. So it was said based on existence being a positive attribute, which is false, otherwise it would be either inside the quiddity or outside, both false as previously shown. Also, if it were positive, it would be equal in positivity to other quiddities but different in particularity, so its existence is other than its quiddity. Then the quiddity's being characterized by its existence: if it is necessary, then necessity would be another necessity ad infinitum; and if it is not necessary, it would be contingent, and the Necessary in Himself is more deserving of being contingent—this is a [vicious] circle.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a proof that necessity-by-essence cannot be a shared attribute between two beings (e.g., two necessary beings). If it were shared, each being would be composite of a common factor (necessity) and a distinguishing factor. Composition implies either no necessary connection between parts—then the composite is caused by an external cause, contradicting necessity—or a necessary connection. If the essence entails necessity, then necessity depends on essence, violating simplicity. If necessity entails the essence, then each necessary being would be identical to what it is not. The further argument uses the nature of existence as a positive attribute: if existence is positive, then the quiddity would be distinct from existence, leading to an infinite regress or contingency of the necessary. All options lead to contradiction, so necessity cannot be shared.

Key Terms
وجوب بالذات
تركيب
امتياز
اشتراك
ثبوتي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that necessary existence is an attribute like any other that can be shared among multiple beings, similar to how 'whiteness' can be shared.
Correction: The argument shows that sharing necessary existence leads to composition, dependence, and regress, which are inconsistent with the definition of necessary being. Unlike accidental attributes, necessary existence is the being itself, not an added attribute.

Checkpoint
If necessity-by-essence is shared between two beings, what problem arises?
A) Each being becomes simple.
B) Each being becomes composite, leading to dependence or circularity.
C) Necessity becomes accidental.
D) The beings become identical.

Key Takeaway
Necessary existence is unique and cannot be shared; any attempt to share it results in logical contradictions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof shows that God's necessary existence cannot be shared or composed. Reflect: In your heart, do you ever treat God as one among many influences in your life, as if His necessity depends on something else? How can you cultivate the certainty that He alone is self-sufficient and independent?
?
The argument traces how sharing necessity leads to absurdity. Consider your own reliance on God: Are there areas in your life where you rely on created beings as if they were necessary for you, forgetting that only God is truly necessary? What practical steps will you take today to redirect that reliance solely to Him?
?
If existence were a positive attribute, it would lead to infinite regress or contingency. Think about your own existence: Does it feel contingent, dependent on God's continuous creative act? How does this awareness shape your gratitude and dependence on Him each moment?
